## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress sigma, strain epsilon, and temperature T, which is a classic setup for constitutive laws in solid mechanics describing elastic/plastic response with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield, and hardening (thermoelasticity and thermoplasticity). Likely relationships include sigma increasing with epsilon (elasticity/hardening) and decreasing with T (thermal softening) plus possible thermal-strain offsets.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic stiffness): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-activated stiffness change; c1 often negative for softening)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion shifts the stress-free strain)
- Polynomial elastic nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate nonlinearity with T-dependent coefficients)
- Hollomon power-law hardening (isothermal): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (plastic flow curve; c1 can represent pre-strain/offset)
- Temperature-softened power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (flow stress decreases with T while retaining power-law strain hardening)
- Ludwik-type law: sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield-like offset plus strain hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that saturates at large strain)
- Temperature-dependent Voce hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (saturation stress and/or hardening rate varies with T)
- Ramberg–Osgood implicit form (rearranged for sigma): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (common elastic+plastic strain decomposition; used when sigma–epsilon is nonlinear)
- Eyring-like hyperbolic sine flow form: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (captures rapid initial hardening then slower increase; temperature scales the stress level)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength often appears as multiplicative exp(c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) factors on an otherwise strain-driven law for sigma(epsilon).
- Thermal expansion introduces an effective strain shift: sigma depends on (epsilon - c*(T - T0)), producing near-parallel sigma–epsilon curves at different T.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition is commonly represented by an additive offset in sigma (yield-like c0) plus a nonlinear hardening term in epsilon.
- Hardening saturation at large epsilon is well captured by (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) terms, reflecting approach to a limiting stress.
- Initial rapid increase followed by gradual hardening can be modeled by log(1 + c*epsilon) or asinh(c*epsilon) structures (concave-down sigma vs epsilon).
- If curves at different T collapse by vertical scaling, prefer sigma = g(T) * f(epsilon); if they shift horizontally, prefer sigma = f(epsilon - h(T)).
- When temperature changes both the slope at small strain and the large-strain level, use T-dependent coefficients in multiple terms (e.g., both linear-in-epsilon and saturation terms scaled by T).
- If sigma approaches linearity at very small epsilon but becomes nonlinear later, combine a linear elastic term plus a nonlinear hardening term rather than a single global polynomial.

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + c4*(T - c5)*log(epsilon + c6)
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `6.531365700567425*epsilon**3 - 0.6867651335523405*(T - 289.08080514174986) + 3.018423785145038*(T - 289.08080514174986)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Expanding the GT:
- `6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.6868*T + 198.55 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 872.56*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `6.531*epsilon^3 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 0.6868*T - 872.56*log(epsilon+1) + 198.55`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. **epsilon^3** (polynomial)
2. **T*log(epsilon+1)** (product of T and log)
3. **T** (linear in T)
4. **log(epsilon+1)** (logarithm)
5. **constant**

Now I need to check each candidate. Most candidates are built from rational functions of epsilon (like `epsilon/(c*epsilon+c)` and `1/(c*epsilon+c)`), polynomials in epsilon and T, terms like `1/T`, `epsilon/T`, and occasionally `exp`, `sin`, `cos`, `log`.

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `log(epsilon+1)` and `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are logarithmic basis functions. For a candidate to match, it must somehow produce logarithmic terms. Rational functions, polynomials, exponentials, and trigonometric functions cannot produce `log` terms.

Let me scan for candidates containing `log`:
- **Candidate 27:** contains `log(c8*Abs(epsilon) + 1)` — this has a log term!

Let me check Candidate 27:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2 + c3*epsilon/(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*Abs(epsilon) + 1)`

The log term is multiplied by `exp(T*c7)`. For this to match `T*log(epsilon+1)`, we'd need `exp(T*c7)` to be linear in T, which is impossible (exponential ≠ linear). If c7=0, then `exp(0)=1`, giving just `c6*log(...)`, which provides the `log(epsilon+1)` term but NOT the `T*log(epsilon+1)` term. So Candidate 27 cannot match.

No other candidate contains `log`. Let me verify there's no way to produce `log` from other functions — there isn't. Rational functions are ratios of polynomials, `exp` is exponential, `sin`/`cos` are trigonometric. None can produce logarithmic behavior.

Since the GT fundamentally requires `T*log(epsilon+1)` and `log(epsilon+1)` as basis functions, and no candidate can produce these terms, **none of the candidates match**.

Let me do a final check on all candidates with special functions:
- Candidates with `exp(c/T)` or `exp(T*c)`: exponentials, not logs
- Candidates with `sin`, `cos`: trigonometric, not logs
- Candidate 27: has log but multiplied by exp(T*c), can't produce T*log
- Candidate 26: has `(T+c7)^c8` — power function, not log

None can produce the required `T*log(epsilon+1)` term.
